      <td class="d-block comment-body markdown-body  js-comment-body">
          <p dir="auto">Regarding issue <a class="issue-link js-issue-link" data-error-text="Failed to load title" data-id="34004549" data-permission-text="Title is private" data-url="https://github.com/cure53/DOMPurify/issues/26" data-hovercard-type="issue" data-hovercard-url="/cure53/DOMPurify/issues/26/hovercard" href="https://github.com/cure53/DOMPurify/issues/26">#26</a> and <a class="issue-link js-issue-link" data-error-text="Failed to load title" data-id="35310177" data-permission-text="Title is private" data-url="https://github.com/cure53/DOMPurify/issues/27" data-hovercard-type="pull_request" data-hovercard-url="/cure53/DOMPurify/pull/27/hovercard" href="https://github.com/cure53/DOMPurify/pull/27">#27</a>, I originally held back Common JS style exports and publishing on npm on purpose, as DOMPurify doesn't run on a pure Node.js environment (it does client side with Browserify).</p>
<p dir="auto">I'm still looking for a way to get it to work on Node.js as well. jsdom <a href="https://github.com/tmpvar/jsdom/issues/317" data-hovercard-type="issue" data-hovercard-url="/jsdom/jsdom/issues/317/hovercard">lacks DOM Level 2 Traversal methods</a> like <code class="notranslate">createNodeIterator</code> at the moment, which DOMPurify uses internally.</p>
<p dir="auto">What's currently missing:</p>
<ul class="contains-task-list">
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" checked=""> <code class="notranslate">document.implementation.createHTMLDocument</code><br>
(polyfilled with <code class="notranslate">return jsdom('&lt;html&gt;&lt;body&gt;&lt;/body&gt;&lt;/html&gt;');</code>)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox" checked=""> `window.NodeFilter (extracted the properties needed for DOMPurify from the spec)</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox"> <code class="notranslate">document.createNodeIterator(root, whatToShow, filter, entityReferenceExpansion)</code></li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox"> <code class="notranslate">NodeIterator.nextNode()</code> implementation</li>
<li class="task-list-item"><input type="checkbox" id="" disabled="" class="task-list-item-checkbox"> Setter method for <code class="notranslate">document.body.outerHTML</code></li>
</ul>
      </td>
    </tr>
      <tr class="d-block pl-3 pr-3 pb-3 js-comment-body-error" hidden>

        <a href="#issuecomment-96739023" id="issuecomment-96739023-permalink" class="Link--secondary js-timestamp"><relative-time datetime="2015-04-27T16:55:00Z" class="no-wrap">Apr 27, 2015</relative-time></a>

      <div class="edit-comment-hide">

        <task-lists disabled sortable>
<table class="d-block user-select-contain" data-paste-markdown-skip>
  <tbody class="d-block">
    <tr class="d-block">
      <td class="d-block comment-body markdown-body  js-comment-body">
          <p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/tmpvar/jsdom/blob/master/Changelog.md#520">jsdom 5.2.0</a> has many fixes to make dompurify work. Most html snippets can now be "purified" properly.<br>
Although I have to load dompurify as a script using jsdom.env because dompurify uses a lot of globals. It would be great if I could instantiate dompurify by passing it a <code class="notranslate">Window</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">There are still a few test cases failing though, which would require more work in jsdom. One example is that jsdom currently throws an exception if an attribute is set with an invalid name: <code class="notranslate">foo.innerHTML = "&lt;img id/=' &gt;"</code>. The spec says that resolving parser errors is optional, but it is of course not how the browsers behave. The result is that dompurify is not able to clean up such snippets.</p>
      </td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
</task-lists>

  <tbody class="d-block">
    <tr class="d-block">
      <td class="d-block comment-body markdown-body  js-comment-body">
          <p dir="auto">As for releasing:<br>
I do not think that any XSS attempts will get through if you use jsdom with these unresolved issues. The effects of these issues are:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code class="notranslate">adoptNode</code>, <code class="notranslate">activeElement</code> and maybe others that are not in the test cases may get clobbered if you only filter using jsdom. These are not causing XSS leaks.</li>
<li><del>Invalid CSS in style tags will throw. For example if DOMPurify is used in a node http server, it would give clients a 500 error instead of the sanitized html.</del></li>
<li>The KEEP_CONTENT option does not work at all</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">The only thing I am not sure about yet are the 2 cases (87 and 173) that fail with svg content. I have not looked at those extensively. Perhaps all those need are an additional "expected" value in the test case itself.</p>
<p dir="auto">Here is the output of the test cases: <a href="https://joris-van-der-wel.github.io/DOMPurify-04d7218-on-jsdom-5.4.0.html" rel="nofollow">https://joris-van-der-wel.github.io/DOMPurify-04d7218-on-jsdom-5.4.0.html</a> and here is the script I used to generate this <a href="https://joris-van-der-wel.github.io/DOMPurify-test-jsdom.js" rel="nofollow">https://joris-van-der-wel.github.io/DOMPurify-test-jsdom.js</a></p>
      </td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

          <p dir="auto">I just stumbled upon this problem. I found a lightweight alternative for a simple DOMPurify use-case that works in Node: <a href="https://github.com/leizongmin/js-xss">https://github.com/leizongmin/js-xss</a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import xss from 'xss';

export function sanitizeText(string) {
  // only include whitelisted tags, remove the others
  return xss(string, { whiteList: ['b', 'i', 'strong'], stripIgnoreTag: true });
}"><pre class="notranslate"><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">xss</span> <span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s">'xss'</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">export</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">sanitizeText</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">string</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-c">// only include whitelisted tags, remove the others</span>
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-en">xss</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">string</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> <span class="pl-c1">whiteList</span>: <span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s">'b'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">'i'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">'strong'</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-c1">stripIgnoreTag</span>: <span class="pl-c1">true</span> <span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">It has to be lightweight because I'm using it with server-side rendered React, which runs in Node first but then runs in the browser.</p>
